class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Major cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The most populous city of Siberia, as well as the third most populous city of Russia, is the city of <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk" title="Novosibirsk">Novosibirsk</a>. Other major cities include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barnaul" title="Barnaul">Barnaul</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kemerovo" title="Kemerovo">Kemerovo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Krasnoyarsk" title="Krasnoyarsk">Krasnoyarsk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Novokuznetsk" title="Novokuznetsk">Novokuznetsk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Omsk" title="Omsk">Omsk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tomsk" title="Tomsk">Tomsk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tyumen" title="Tyumen">Tyumen</a></li></ul>\n<p>Wider definitions of Siberia also include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Chelyabinsk" title="Chelyabinsk">Chelyabinsk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk" title="Khabarovsk">Khabarovsk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yekaterinburg" title="Yekaterinburg">Yekaterinburg</a> - Some sources such as <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica">Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica</a> include this city as it lies in the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>. Inhabitants have distanced themselves though saying that there is a difference between Siberian and Urals culture.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif/220px-RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif/330px-RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif/440px-RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif 2x" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="757" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russia is a key <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a> supplier to much of Europe.</div></div></div>\n<p>Siberia is extraordinarily rich in <a href="/wiki/Mineral" title="Mineral">minerals</a>, containing ores of almost all economically valuable <a href="/wiki/Metal" title="Metal">metals</a>. It has some of the world\'s largest deposits of <a href="/wiki/Norilsk#Norilsk-Talnakh_nickel_deposits" title="Norilsk">nickel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molybdenum" title="Molybdenum">molybdenum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diopside" title="Diopside">diopside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, as well as extensive unexploited resources of <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Around 70% of Russia\'s developed <a href="/wiki/List_of_oil_fields" title="List of oil fields">oil fields</a> are in the <a href="/wiki/Khanty-Mansiysk" title="Khanty-Mansiysk">Khanty-Mansiysk</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Russia contains about 40% of the world\'s known resources of <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Norilsk" title="Norilsk">Norilsk</a> deposit in Siberia. <a href="/wiki/Norilsk_Nickel" class="mw-redirect" title="Norilsk Nickel">Norilsk Nickel</a> is the world\'s biggest nickel and <a href="/wiki/Palladium" title="Palladium">palladium</a> producer.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Siberian_agriculture" title="Siberian agriculture">Siberian agriculture</a> is severely restricted by the short growing season of most of the region. However, in the southwest where soils are exceedingly fertile black earths and the climate is a little more moderate, there is extensive cropping of <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rye" title="Rye">rye</a> and <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, along with the grazing of large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>. Elsewhere food production, owing to the poor fertility of the <a href="/wiki/Podzol" title="Podzol">podzolic</a> soils and the extremely short growing seasons, is restricted to the herding of <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">reindeer</a> in the tundra\xe2\x80\x94which has been practiced by natives for over 10,000 years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Siberia has the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forests</a>. Timber remains an important source of revenue, even though many forests in the east have been logged much more rapidly than they are able to recover. The <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a> is one of the two or three richest fisheries in the world owing to its cold currents and very large <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">tidal ranges</a>, and thus Siberia produces over 10% of the world\'s annual fish catch, although fishing has declined somewhat since the collapse of the USSR.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the development of renewable energy in Russia is held back by the lack of a conducive government policy framework,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Siberia still offers special opportunities for off-grid renewable energy developments. Remote parts of Siberia are too costly to connect to central electricity and gas grids, and have therefore historically been supplied with costly diesel, sometimes flown in by helicopter. In such cases renewable energy is often cheaper.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sibselmash_Stadium_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Sibselmash_Stadium_1.jpg/220px-Sibselmash_Stadium_1.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Sibselmash_Stadium_1.jpg/330px-Sibselmash_Stadium_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Sibselmash_Stadium_1.jpg/440px-Sibselmash_Stadium_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3088" data-file-height="1744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sibselmash_Stadium_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">Bandy</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sibselmash_Stadium" title="Sibselmash Stadium">Sibselmash Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk" title="Novosibirsk">Novosibirsk</a>, Siberia\'s biggest city and the third biggest one in Russia</div></div></div>\n<p>Professional football teams include <a href="/wiki/FC_Tom_Tomsk" title="FC Tom Tomsk">FC Tom Tomsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Sibir_Novosibirsk" title="FC Sibir Novosibirsk">FC Sibir Novosibirsk</a> and <a href="/wiki/FK_Yenisey_Krasnoyarsk" class="mw-redirect" title="FK Yenisey Krasnoyarsk">FK Yenisey Krasnoyarsk</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/BC_Yenisey_Krasnoyarsk" class="mw-redirect" title="BC Yenisey Krasnoyarsk">Yenisey Krasnoyarsk</a> basketball team has played in the <a href="/wiki/VTB_United_League" title="VTB United League">VTB United League</a> since 2011\xe2\x80\x9312.\n</p><p>Russia\'s third most popular sport, <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">bandy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> is important in Siberia. In the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Russian_Bandy_Super_League" title="2015\xe2\x80\x9316 Russian Bandy Super League">2015\xe2\x80\x9316 Russian Bandy Super League season</a> <a href="/wiki/Yenisey_Krasnoyarsk_Bandy_Club" title="Yenisey Krasnoyarsk Bandy Club">Yenisey</a> from <a href="/wiki/Krasnoyarsk" title="Krasnoyarsk">Krasnoyarsk</a> became champions for the third year in a row by beating <a href="/wiki/Baykal-Energiya_Irkutsk" class="mw-redirect" title="Baykal-Energiya Irkutsk">Baykal-Energiya</a> from <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a> in the final.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Two or three more teams (depending on the definition of Siberia) play in the Super League, the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Russian_Bandy_Super_League" title="2016\xe2\x80\x9317 Russian Bandy Super League">2016-17</a> champions <a href="/wiki/SKA-Neftyanik_Khabarovsk" class="mw-redirect" title="SKA-Neftyanik Khabarovsk">SKA-Neftyanik</a> from <a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk" title="Khabarovsk">Khabarovsk</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Kuzbass_Kemerovo_Bandy_Club" title="Kuzbass Kemerovo Bandy Club">Kuzbass</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kemerovo" title="Kemerovo">Kemerovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sibselmash_Novosibirsk" class="mw-redirect" title="Sibselmash Novosibirsk">Sibselmash</a> from <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk" title="Novosibirsk">Novosibirsk</a>. In 2007 Kemerovo got Russia\'s first indoor arena specifically built for bandy.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Now Khabarovsk has the world\'s biggest indoor arena specifically built for bandy, <a href="/wiki/Arena_Yerofey" title="Arena Yerofey">Arena Yerofey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> It will be the venue for Division A of the <a href="/wiki/2018_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2018 Bandy World Championship">2018 World Championship</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2019_Winter_Universiade" title="2019 Winter Universiade">2019 Winter Universiade</a> will be hosted by Krasnoyarsk.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Siberia" title="Demographics of Siberia">Demographics of Siberia</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Bukharans" title="Siberian Bukharans">Siberian Bukharans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Siberia" title="Ukrainians in Siberia">Ukrainians in Siberia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Street_Scene_in_Tomsk_-_Russia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Street_Scene_in_Tomsk_-_Russia.JPG/220px-Street_Scene_in_Tomsk_-_Russia.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Street_Scene_in_Tomsk_-_Russia.JPG/330px-Street_Scene_in_Tomsk_-_Russia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Street_Scene_in_Tomsk_-_Russia.JPG/440px-Street_Scene_in_Tomsk_-_Russia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Street_Scene_in_Tomsk_-_Russia.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tomsk" title="Tomsk">Tomsk</a>, one of the oldest Siberian cities, was founded in 1604.</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Census_(2010)" title="Russian Census (2010)">Russian Census of 2010</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Federal_District" title="Siberian Federal District">Siberian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Far_Eastern_Federal_District" title="Far Eastern Federal District">Far Eastern</a> Federal Districts, located entirely east of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>, together have a population of about 25.6 million. <a href="/wiki/Tyumen_Oblast" title="Tyumen Oblast">Tyumen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kurgan_Oblast" title="Kurgan Oblast">Kurgan</a> Oblasts, which are geographically in Siberia but administratively part of the <a href="/wiki/Urals_Federal_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Urals Federal District">Urals Federal District</a>, together have a population of about 4.3 million. Thus, the whole region of Asian Russia (or Siberia in the broadest usage of the term) is home to approximately 30 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> It has a population density of about three people per square kilometre.\n</p><p>All Siberians are Russian citizens, and of these Russian citizens of Siberia, most are Slavic-origin <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> and russified <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Russia" title="Ukrainians in Russia">Ukrainians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The remaining Russian citizens of Siberia consists of other groups of non-indigenous ethnic origins and those of indigenous Siberian origin.\n</p><p>Among the largest non-Slavic group of Russian citizens of Siberia are the approximately 400,000 ethnic <a href="/wiki/Volga_Germans" title="Volga Germans">Volga Germans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The original indigenous groups of Siberia, including <a href="/wiki/Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> groups such as <a href="/wiki/Buryats" title="Buryats">Buryats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuvinians" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuvinians">Tuvinians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">Yakuts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Tatars" title="Siberian Tatars">Siberian Tatars</a> still mostly reside in Siberia, though they are minorities outnumbered by all other non-indigenous Siberians. Indeed, Slavic-origin Russians by themselves outnumber all of the indigenous peoples combined, both in Siberia as a whole and its cities, except in the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Tuva" title="Tuva">Tuva</a>.\n</p><p>Slavic-origin Russians make up the majority in the Buryat, <a href="/wiki/Sakha_Republic" title="Sakha Republic">Sakha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Altai_Republic" title="Altai Republic">Altai Republics</a>, outnumbering the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Buryats" title="Buryats">Buryats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">Sakha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Altai_people" title="Altai people">Altai</a>. The Buryat make up only 25% of their own republic, and the Sakha and Altai each are only one-third, and the Chukchi, <a href="/wiki/Evenks" title="Evenks">Evenk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khanty_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Khanty people">Khanti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mansi_people" title="Mansi people">Mansi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nenets_people" title="Nenets people">Nenets</a> are outnumbered by non-indigenous peoples by 90% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the 2002 census there are 500,000 <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Tatars" title="Siberian Tatars">Tatars in Siberia</a>, but of these, 300,000 are <a href="/wiki/Volga_Tatars" title="Volga Tatars">Volga Tatars</a> who also settled in Siberia during periods of colonization and are thus also non-indigenous Siberians, in contrast to the 200,000 Siberian Tatars which are indigenous to Siberia.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of the indigenous Siberians, the <a href="/wiki/Buryats" title="Buryats">Buryats</a>, numbering approximately 500,000, are the most numerous group in Siberia, and they are mainly concentrated in their homeland, the <a href="/wiki/Buryatia" title="Buryatia">Buryat Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Russia#Ethnic_groups" title="Demographics of Russia">2002 census</a> there were 443,852 indigenous <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">Yakuts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> indigenous to Siberia include <a href="/wiki/Ket_people" title="Ket people">Kets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evenks" title="Evenks">Evenks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chukchis" class="mw-redirect" title="Chukchis">Chukchis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koryaks" title="Koryaks">Koryaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yupik_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Yupik peoples">Yupiks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yukaghirs" class="mw-redirect" title="Yukaghirs">Yukaghirs</a>.\n</p><p>About seventy percent of Siberia\'s people live in cities, mainly in apartments. Many people also live in rural areas, in simple, spacious, log houses. <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk" title="Novosibirsk">Novosibirsk</a> is the largest city in Siberia, with a population of about 1.5 million. <a href="/wiki/Tobolsk" title="Tobolsk">Tobolsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomsk" title="Tomsk">Tomsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyumen" title="Tyumen">Tyumen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krasnoyarsk" title="Krasnoyarsk">Krasnoyarsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Omsk" title="Omsk">Omsk</a> are the older, historical centers.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA,_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%2C_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/170px-%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%2C_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%2C_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/255px-%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%2C_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%2C_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg/340px-%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA%2C_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2431" data-file-height="3241" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A5%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%81%D0%BA,_%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%80.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Transfiguration_Cathedral,_Khabarovsk" title="Transfiguration Cathedral, Khabarovsk">Transfiguration Cathedral, Khabarovsk</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Shamanism_in_Siberia" title="Shamanism in Siberia">Shamanism in Siberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Russia" title="Religion in Russia">Religion in Russia</a></div>\n<p>There are a variety of beliefs throughout Siberia, including <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christianity</a>, other denominations of Christianity, <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan Buddhism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Federal_District" title="Siberian Federal District">Siberian Federal District</a> alone has an estimation of 250,000 Muslims.\nAn estimated 70,000 <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Russia_and_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Jews in Russia and the Soviet Union">Jews</a> live in Siberia,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> some in the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Autonomous_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish Autonomous Region">Jewish Autonomous Region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The predominant religious group is the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>.\n</p><p>Tradition regards Siberia the archetypal home of <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">shamanism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polytheism" title="Polytheism">polytheism</a> is popular.<sup id="cite_ref-locclass_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-locclass-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> These native sacred practices are considered by the tribes to be very ancient. There are records of Siberian tribal healing practices dating back to the 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The vast territory of Siberia has many different local traditions of gods. These include: <a href="/wiki/Ak_Ana" title="Ak Ana">Ak Ana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anapel" title="Anapel">Anapel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bugady_Musun" title="Bugady Musun">Bugady Musun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kara-Khitan_Khanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Kara-Khitan Khanate">Kara Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khaltesh-Anki" title="Khaltesh-Anki">Khaltesh-Anki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kini%27je" title="Kini&#39;je">Kini\'je</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ku%27urkil" title="Ku&#39;urkil">Ku\'urkil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nga_(god)" title="Nga (god)">Nga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nu%27tenut" title="Nu&#39;tenut">Nu\'tenut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Numi-Torem" class="mw-redirect" title="Numi-Torem">Numi-Torem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Numi-Turum" class="mw-redirect" title="Numi-Turum">Numi-Turum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yukaghir" class="mw-redirect" title="Yukaghir">Pon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pugu_(deity)" title="Pugu (deity)">Pugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Todote" title="Todote">Todote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toko%27yoto" title="Toko&#39;yoto">Toko\'yoto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomam" title="Tomam">Tomam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xaya_Iccita" title="Xaya Iccita">Xaya Iccita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zonget" title="Zonget">Zonget</a>. Places with sacred areas include <a href="/wiki/Olkhon" class="mw-redirect" title="Olkhon">Olkhon</a>, an island in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Many cities in northern Siberia, such as <a href="/wiki/Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky" title="Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky">Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky</a>, cannot be reached by road, as there are virtually none connecting from other major cities in Russia or Asia. The best way to tour Siberia is through the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a>. The Trans-Siberian Railway operates from Moscow in the west to <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a> in the east. Cities that are located far from the railway are best reached by air or by the separate <a href="/wiki/Baikal_Amur_Mainline" class="mw-redirect" title="Baikal Amur Mainline">Baikal-Amur-Railway</a> (BAM).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Stroganina" title="Stroganina">Stroganina</a> is a raw fish dish of the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous people">indigenous people</a> of northern Arctic Siberia made from raw, thin, long-sliced frozen fish.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> It is a popular dish with native Siberians.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Siberia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Siberian_regionalism" title="Siberian regionalism">Siberian regionalism</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2015-10-11</span></span>. <q>Of the spread of Islam among the Tatars of Siberia, we have a few particulars. It was not until the latter half of the sixteenth century that it gained a footing in this country, but even before this period Muhammadan missionaries had from time to time made their way into Siberia with the hope of winning the heathen population over to the acceptance of their faith, but the majority of them met with a martyr\'s death. When Siberia came under Muhammadan rule, in the reign of <a href="/wiki/Kuchum_Khan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kuchum Khan">Kuchum Khan</a>, the graves of seven of these missionaries were discovered [...]. [...] Kuchum Khan [...] made every effort for the conversion of his subjects, and sent to Bukhara asking for missionaries to assist him in this pious undertaking.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Preaching+of+Islam%3A+A+History+of+the+Propagation+of+the+Muslim+Faith&amp;rft.place=Westminster&amp;rft.pages=206-207&amp;rft.pub=Archibald+Constable+and+Company&amp;rft.date=1896&amp;rft.aulast=Arnold&amp;rft.aufirst=Thomas+Walker&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DqxsVAAAAYAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASiberia" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-70">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090827113526/http://www.fjc.ru/news/newsArticle.asp?AID=136974">"Planting Jewish roots in Siberia"</a>.
